					<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading mw-first-heading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Open source</span></h1>
							
<div id="p-lang-btn" class="vector-dropdown mw-portlet mw-portlet-lang"  >
	<input type="checkbox" id="p-lang-btn-checkbox" role="button" aria-haspopup="true" data-event-name="ui.dropdown-p-lang-btn" class="vector-dropdown-checkbox mw-interlanguage-selector" aria-label="Go to an article in another language. Available in 61 languages"   >

	</label>

href="https://ur.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D8%A2%D8%B2%D8%A7%D8%AF_%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%AF%D8%B1" title="آزاد مصدر – Urdu" lang="ur" hreflang="ur" data-title="آزاد مصدر" data-language-autonym="اردو" data-language-local-name="Urdu" class="interlanguage-link-target"><span>اردو</span></a></li><li class="interlanguage-link interwiki-vi mw-list-item"><a href="https://vi.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ngu%E1%BB%93n_m%E1%BB%9F" title="Nguồn mở – Vietnamese" lang="vi" hreflang="vi" data-title="Nguồn mở" data-language-autonym="Tiếng Việt" data-language-local-name="Vietnamese" class="interlanguage-link-target"><span>Tiếng Việt</span></a></li><li class="interlanguage-link interwiki-yi mw-list-item"><a href="https://yi.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D7%90%D7%A4%D7%A2%D7%A0%D7%A2%D7%A8_%D7%A7%D7%90%D7%93" title="אפענער קאד – Yiddish" lang="yi" hreflang="yi" data-title="אפענער קאד" data-language-autonym="ייִדיש" data-language-local-name="Yiddish" class="interlanguage-link-target"><span>ייִדיש</span></a></li><li class="interlanguage-link interwiki-zh mw-list-item"><a data-language-local-name="Chinese" class="interlanguage-link-target"><span>中文</span></a></li>

				<div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body" aria-labelledby="firstHeading" data-mw-ve-target-container>
					<div class="vector-body-before-content">
							<div class="mw-indicators">
		</div>

						<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
					</div>
					<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"></div></div>
					
					
					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Source code made freely available</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Open_Source_Initiative.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Open_Source_Initiative.svg/220px-Open_Source_Initiative.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="289" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Open_Source_Initiative.svg/330px-Open_Source_Initiative.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Open_Source_Initiative.svg/440px-Open_Source_Initiative.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="585" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption>Open Source Initiative logo</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Open source</b> is <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a> that is made freely available for possible modification and redistribution. Products include permission to use and view the source code,<sup id="cite_ref-Open_Source_Org.,_2007_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Open_Source_Org.,_2007-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> design documents,<sup id="cite_ref-Diffingo_Solutions_Inc.,_2008_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diffingo_Solutions_Inc.,_2008-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or content of the product. The <b>open source model</b> is a decentralized software development model that encourages open collaboration.<sup id="cite_ref-LevinePrietula2013_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LevinePrietula2013-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
A main principle of open source software development is peer production, with products such as source code, blueprints, and documentation freely available to the public. The open source movement in software began as a response to the limitations of proprietary code. The model is used for projects such as in open source appropriate technology,<sup id="cite_ref-Pearce2012_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pearce2012-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and open source drug discovery.<sup id="cite_ref-business-standard.com_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-business-standard.com-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OpenWetWare_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OpenWetWare-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Open source promotes universal access via an open-source or free license to a product's design or blueprint, and universal redistribution of that design or blueprint.<sup id="cite_ref-LakhaniVonHippel2003_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LakhaniVonHippel2003-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GerberMolefo2010_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GerberMolefo2010-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Before the phrase <i>open source</i> became widely adopted, developers and producers used a variety of other terms, such as <i>free software</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Shareware" title="Shareware">shareware</a></i>, and <i>public domain software</i>. <i>Open source</i> gained hold with the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The open-source software movement arose to clarify copyright, licensing, domain, and consumer issues.
</p><p>Generally, open source refers to a computer program in which the source code is available to the general public for use or modification from its original design. Code is released under the terms of a software license. Depending on the license terms, others may then download, modify, and publish their version (fork) back to the community. Many large formal institutions have sprung up to support the development of the open-source movement, including the Apache Software Foundation, which supports community projects such as the open-source framework  and the open-source HTTP server Apache HTTP.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_free_and_open-source_software" title="History of free and open-source software">History of free and open-source software</a></div>
<p>The sharing of technical information predates the Internet and the personal computer considerably. For instance, in the early years of automobile development a group of capital <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopolists</a> owned the rights to a <a href="/wiki/2_cycle" class="mw-redirect" title="2 cycle">2-cycle</a> gasoline-engine patent originally filed by <a href="/wiki/George_B._Selden" title="George B. Selden">George B. Selden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-carculture_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carculture-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By controlling this patent, they were able to monopolize the industry and force car manufacturers to adhere to their demands, or risk a lawsuit.
</p><p>In 1911, independent automaker <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a> won a challenge to <a href="/wiki/George_B._Selden#The_Selden_patent" title="George B. Selden">the Selden patent</a>. The result was that the Selden patent became virtually worthless and a new association (which would eventually become the Motor Vehicle Manufacturers Association) was formed.<sup id="cite_ref-carculture_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carculture-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The new association instituted a cross-licensing agreement among all US automotive manufacturers: although each company would develop technology and file patents, these patents were shared openly and without the exchange of money among all the manufacturers.<sup id="cite_ref-carculture_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carculture-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the time the US entered <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, 92 Ford patents and 515 patents from other companies were being shared among these manufacturers, without any exchange of money (or lawsuits).<sup id="cite_ref-carculture_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carculture-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Early instances of the free sharing of source code include <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>'s source releases of its <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating systems</a> and other programs in the 1950s and 1960s, and the <a href="/wiki/SHARE_(computing)" title="SHARE (computing)">SHARE</a> user group that formed to facilitate the exchange of software.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated172_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated172-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Beginning in the 1960s, <a href="/wiki/ARPANET" title="ARPANET">ARPANET</a> researchers used an open "<a href="/wiki/Request_for_Comments" title="Request for Comments">Request for Comments</a>" (RFC) process to encourage feedback in early telecommunication network protocols. This led to the birth of the early Internet in 1969.
</p><p>The sharing of source code on the Internet began when the Internet was relatively primitive, with software distributed via <a href="/wiki/UUCP" title="UUCP">UUCP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usenet" title="Usenet">Usenet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_Relay_Chat" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet Relay Chat">IRC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gopher_(protocol)" title="Gopher (protocol)">Gopher</a>. <a href="/wiki/BSD" class="mw-redirect" title="BSD">BSD</a>, for example, was first widely distributed by posts to comp.os.linux on the Usenet, which is also where its development was discussed. <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> followed in this model.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Open_source_as_a_term">Open source as a term</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Open source as a term"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Open source as a term emerged in the late 1990s by a group of people in the free software movement who were critical of the political agenda and moral philosophy implied in the term "free software" and sought to reframe the discourse to reflect a more commercially minded position.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition, the ambiguity of the term "free software" was seen as discouraging business adoption.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-infoworld1983_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infoworld1983-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, the ambiguity of the word "free" exists primarily in English as it can refer to cost. The group included <a href="/wiki/Christine_Peterson" title="Christine Peterson">Christine Peterson</a>, Todd Anderson, <a href="/wiki/Larry_Augustin" title="Larry Augustin">Larry Augustin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Hall_(programmer)" title="Jon Hall (programmer)">Jon Hall</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sam_Ockman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sam Ockman (page does not exist)">Sam Ockman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Tiemann" title="Michael Tiemann">Michael Tiemann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_S._Raymond" title="Eric S. Raymond">Eric S. Raymond</a>. Peterson suggested "open source" at a meeting<sup id="cite_ref-osihistory_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osihistory-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> held at <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">Palo Alto, California</a>, in reaction to <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Communications_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Netscape Communications Corporation">Netscape</a>'s announcement in January 1998 of a source code release for <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Navigator" title="Netscape Navigator">Navigator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Conflict_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conflict-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Linus_Torvalds" title="Linus Torvalds">Linus Torvalds</a> gave his support the following day, and Phil Hughes backed the term in <i><a href="/wiki/Linux_Journal" title="Linux Journal">Linux Journal</a></i>. Richard Stallman, the founder of the Free Software Foundation (FSF) in 1985, quickly decided against endorsing the term.<sup id="cite_ref-osihistory_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osihistory-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rmsdissent_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rmsdissent-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The FSF's goal was to promote the development and use of free software, which they defined as software that grants users the freedom to run, study, share, and modify the code. This concept is similar to open source but places a greater emphasis on the ethical and political aspects of software freedom. Netscape released its source code under the Netscape Public License and later under the <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Public_License" title="Mozilla Public License">Mozilla Public License</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Muffatto000_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muffatto000-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Raymond was especially active in the effort to popularize the new term. He made the first public call to the free software community to adopt it in February 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-raymondCall_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raymondCall-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Shortly after, he founded The Open Source Initiative in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Perens" title="Bruce Perens">Bruce Perens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-osihistory_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osihistory-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The term gained further visibility through an event organized in April 1998 by technology publisher . Originally titled the "Freeware Summit" and later known as the "Open Source Summit",<sup id="cite_ref-opensourcesummit_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opensourcesummit-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the event was attended by the leaders of many of the most important free and open-source projects, including Linus Torvalds, Larry Wall, Brian Behlendorf, Eric Allman, Guido van Rossum, Michael Tiemann, Paul Vixie, Jamie Zawinski, and Eric Raymond. At that meeting, alternatives to the term "free software" were discussed. Tiemann argued for "sourceware" as a new term, while Raymond argued for "open source." The assembled developers took a vote, and the winner was announced at a press conference the same evening.<sup id="cite_ref-opensourcesummit_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opensourcesummit-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economics">Economics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Economics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Open-source_economics" title="Open-source economics">Open-source economics</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Anwendungsgebiete_Open_Source.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Anwendungsgebiete_Open_Source.svg/220px-Anwendungsgebiete_Open_Source.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="311" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Anwendungsgebiete_Open_Source.svg/330px-Anwendungsgebiete_Open_Source.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Anwendungsgebiete_Open_Source.svg/440px-Anwendungsgebiete_Open_Source.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="1052" /></a><figcaption>Area of application of open-source software<sup id="cite_ref-:0_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Einsatzgr%C3%BCnde_Open_Source.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Einsatzgr%C3%BCnde_Open_Source.svg/250px-Einsatzgr%C3%BCnde_Open_Source.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Einsatzgr%C3%BCnde_Open_Source.svg/330px-Einsatzgr%C3%BCnde_Open_Source.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Einsatzgr%C3%BCnde_Open_Source.svg/500px-Einsatzgr%C3%BCnde_Open_Source.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="526" /></a><figcaption>Survey on the reasons for using Open Source in 200 Swiss organizations<sup id="cite_ref-:0_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>Some economists agree that open-source is an <a href="/wiki/Information_good" title="Information good">information good</a><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or "knowledge good" with original work involving a significant amount of time, money, and effort. The cost of reproducing the work is low enough that additional users may be added at zero or near zero cost&#160;&#8211;&#32;this is referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Marginal_cost" title="Marginal cost">marginal cost</a> of a product. <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">Copyright</a> creates a monopoly so that the price charged to consumers can be significantly higher than the marginal cost of production. This allows the author to recoup the cost of making the original work. Copyright thus creates access costs for consumers who value the work more than the marginal cost but less than the initial production cost. Access costs also pose problems for authors who wish to create a <a href="/wiki/Derivative_work" title="Derivative work">derivative work</a>—such as a copy of a software program modified to fix a bug or add a feature, or a <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remix</a> of a song—but are unable or unwilling to pay the copyright holder for the right to do so.
</p><p>Being organized as effectively a "<a href="/wiki/Consumers%27_cooperative" class="mw-redirect" title="Consumers&#39; cooperative">consumers' cooperative</a>", open source eliminates some of the access costs of consumers and creators of derivative works by reducing the restrictions of copyright. Basic economic theory predicts that lower costs would lead to higher consumption and also more frequent creation of derivative works. Organizations such as <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a> host websites where individuals can file for alternative "licenses", or levels of restriction, for their works.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
These self-made protections free the general society of the costs of policing copyright infringement.
</p><p>Others argue that since consumers do not pay for their copies, creators are unable to recoup the initial cost of production and thus have little economic incentive to create in the first place. By this argument, consumers would lose out because some of the goods they would otherwise purchase would not be available. In practice, content producers can choose whether to adopt a proprietary license and charge for copies, or an open license. Some goods which require large amounts of professional research and development, such as the <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceutical industry</a> (which depends largely on patents, not copyright for intellectual property protection) are almost exclusively proprietary, although increasingly sophisticated technologies are being developed on open-source principles.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>There is evidence that open-source development creates enormous value.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example, in the context of <a href="/wiki/Open-source_hardware" title="Open-source hardware">open-source hardware</a> design, digital designs are shared for free and anyone with access to digital manufacturing technologies (e.g. <a href="/wiki/RepRap" title="RepRap">RepRap</a> 3D printers) can replicate the product for the cost of materials.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The original sharer may receive feedback and potentially improvements on the original design from the <a href="/wiki/Peer_production" title="Peer production">peer production</a> community.
</p><p>Many open-source projects have a high economic value. According to the Battery Open Source Software Index (BOSS), the ten economically most important open-source projects are:<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-techcrunch.com_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techcrunch.com-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
