</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Licensing_alternatives">Licensing alternatives</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Licensing alternatives"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Business_models_for_open-source_software" title="Business models for open-source software">Business models for open-source software</a></div>
<p>Alternative arrangements have also been shown to result in good creation outside of the proprietary license model. Examples include:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li><figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikipedia-logo-v2-en.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Wikipedia-logo-v2-en.svg/125px-Wikipedia-logo-v2-en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="125" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Wikipedia-logo-v2-en.svg/188px-Wikipedia-logo-v2-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Wikipedia-logo-v2-en.svg/250px-Wikipedia-logo-v2-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="135" data-file-height="155" /></a><figcaption>Wikipedia is an example of a global application of the open-source model.</figcaption></figure>Creation for its own sake – For example, Wikipedia editors add content for recreation. Artists have a drive to create. Both communities benefit from free starting material.</li>
<li>Voluntary after-the-fact donations – used by <a href="/wiki/Shareware" title="Shareware">shareware</a>, <a href="/wiki/Street_performer" class="mw-redirect" title="Street performer">street performers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public broadcasting</a> in the United States.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>Patron – For example, <a href="/wiki/Open-access" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-access">open-access</a> publishing relies on institutional and government funding of research faculty, who also have a professional incentive to publish for reputation and career advancement. Works of the US government are automatically released into the <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Freemium" title="Freemium">Freemium</a> – Give away a limited version for free and charge for a premium version (potentially using a <a href="/wiki/Dual_license" class="mw-redirect" title="Dual license">dual license</a>).</li>
<li>Give away the product and charge something related – charge for support of open-source <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_software" title="Enterprise software">enterprise software</a>, give away music but charge for concert admission.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>Give away work to gain market share – used by artists, in corporate software to spoil a dominant competitor (for example in the <a href="/wiki/Browser_wars" title="Browser wars">browser wars</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Android_operating_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Android operating system">Android operating system</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>For own use – Businesses or individual software developers often create software to solve a problem, bearing the full cost of initial creation. They will then open source the solution, and benefit from the improvements others make for their own needs. Communalizing the maintenance burden distributes the cost across more users; <a href="/wiki/Free_rider_problem" class="mw-redirect" title="Free rider problem">free riders</a> can also benefit without undermining the creation process.</li>
<li>Blockchain based licensing. Developers register their contributions on a blockchain and when usage licenses are generated the revenue is shared through the blockchain.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Open_collaboration">Open collaboration</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Open collaboration"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Open_collaboration" title="Open collaboration">Open collaboration</a></div>
<p>The open-source model is a decentralized <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">software development</a> model that encourages <a href="/wiki/Open_collaboration" title="Open collaboration">open collaboration</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-LevinePrietula2013_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LevinePrietula2013-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> meaning "any system of innovation or production that relies on goal-oriented yet loosely coordinated participants who interact to create a product (or service) of economic value, which they make available to contributors and noncontributors alike."<sup id="cite_ref-LevinePrietula2013_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LevinePrietula2013-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A main principle of <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software_development" title="Open-source software development">open-source software development</a> is <a href="/wiki/Peer_production" title="Peer production">peer production</a>, with products such as source code, <a href="/wiki/Blueprint" title="Blueprint">blueprints</a>, and documentation freely available to the public. The open-source movement in software began as a response to the limitations of proprietary code. The model is used for projects such as in <a href="/wiki/Open-source_appropriate_technology" title="Open-source appropriate technology">open-source appropriate technology</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Pearce2012_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pearce2012-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and open-source drug discovery.<sup id="cite_ref-business-standard.com_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-business-standard.com-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OpenWetWare_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OpenWetWare-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The open-source model for software development inspired the use of the term to refer to other forms of open collaboration, such as in <a href="/wiki/Internet_forum" title="Internet forum">Internet forums</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-LakhaniVonHippel2003_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LakhaniVonHippel2003-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mailing_list" title="Mailing list">mailing lists</a><sup id="cite_ref-Jarvenpaa,_S._L._2008_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvenpaa,_S._L._2008-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Online_communities" class="mw-redirect" title="Online communities">online communities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Faraj,_S._2011_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faraj,_S._2011-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Open collaboration is also thought to be the operating principle underlining a gamut of diverse ventures, including <a href="/wiki/TEDx" class="mw-redirect" title="TEDx">TEDx</a> and Wikipedia.<sup id="cite_ref-kurzweilai.net_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kurzweilai.net-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Open collaboration is the principle underlying <a href="/wiki/Peer_production" title="Peer production">peer production</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mass_collaboration" title="Mass collaboration">mass collaboration</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikinomics" title="Wikinomics">wikinomics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LevinePrietula2013_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LevinePrietula2013-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was observed initially in open-source software, but can also be found in many other instances, such as in <a href="/wiki/Internet_forum" title="Internet forum">Internet forums</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-LakhaniVonHippel2003_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LakhaniVonHippel2003-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mailing_list" title="Mailing list">mailing lists</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Jarvenpaa,_S._L._2008_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvenpaa,_S._L._2008-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Internet communities,<sup id="cite_ref-Faraj,_S._2011_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faraj,_S._2011-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and many instances of <a href="/wiki/Open_content" class="mw-redirect" title="Open content">open content</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons_license" title="Creative Commons license">Creative Commons</a>. It also explains some instances of <a href="/wiki/Crowdsourcing" title="Crowdsourcing">crowdsourcing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Collaborative_consumption" title="Collaborative consumption">collaborative consumption</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Open_innovation" title="Open innovation">open innovation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LevinePrietula2013_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LevinePrietula2013-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Riehle et al. define open collaboration as collaboration based on three principles of <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meritocracy" title="Meritocracy">meritocracy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Self-organization" title="Self-organization">self-organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RiehleEllenberger2009_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RiehleEllenberger2009-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Levine and Prietula define open collaboration as "any system of innovation or production that relies on goal-oriented yet loosely coordinated participants who interact to create a product (or service) of economic value, which they make available to contributors and noncontributors alike."<sup id="cite_ref-LevinePrietula2013_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LevinePrietula2013-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This definition captures multiple instances, all joined by similar principles. For example, all of the elements – goods of economic value, open access to contribute and consume, interaction and exchange, purposeful yet loosely coordinated work – are present in an open-source software project, in Wikipedia, or in a user forum or community. They can also be present in a commercial website that is based on <a href="/wiki/User-generated_content" title="User-generated content">user-generated content</a>. In all of these instances of open collaboration, anyone can contribute and anyone can freely partake in the fruits of sharing, which are produced by interacting participants who are loosely coordinated.
</p><p>An annual conference dedicated to the research and practice of open collaboration is the International Symposium on Wikis and Open Collaboration (OpenSym, formerly WikiSym).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As per its website, the group defines open collaboration as "collaboration that is egalitarian (everyone can join, no principled or artificial barriers to participation exist), meritocratic (decisions and status are merit-based rather than imposed) and self-organizing (processes adapt to people rather than people adapt to pre-defined processes)."<sup id="cite_ref-Opensym_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Opensym-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Open-source_license">Open-source license</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Open-source license"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Open-source_license" title="Open-source license">Open-source license</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_free-content_licences" title="List of free-content licences">List of free-content licences</a></div>
<p>Open source promotes universal access via an <a href="/wiki/Open-source_license" title="Open-source license">open-source</a> or <a href="/wiki/Free_license" title="Free license">free license</a> to a product's design or blueprint, and universal redistribution of that design or blueprint.<sup id="cite_ref-LakhaniVonHippel2003_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LakhaniVonHippel2003-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GerberMolefo2010_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GerberMolefo2010-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Before the phrase <i>open source</i> became widely adopted, developers and producers used a variety of other terms. <i>Open source</i> gained hold in part due to the rise of the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software_movement" title="Open-source software movement">open-source software movement</a> arose to clarify <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">copyright</a>, <a href="/wiki/License" title="License">licensing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain</a>, and consumer issues.
</p><p>An open-source license is a type of <a href="/wiki/License_compatibility" title="License compatibility">license</a> for computer software and other products that allows the <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a>, blueprint or design to be used, modified or shared (with or without modification) under defined terms and conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Popp2_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Popp2-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This allows end users and commercial companies to review and modify the source code, blueprint or design for their own customization, curiosity or troubleshooting needs. Open-source licensed software is mostly available <a href="/wiki/Freeware" title="Freeware">free</a> of charge, though this does not necessarily have to be the case. Licenses which only permit non-commercial redistribution or modification of the source code for personal use only are generally not considered as open-source licenses. However, open-source licenses may have some restrictions, particularly regarding the expression of respect to the origin of software, such as a requirement to preserve the name of the authors and a copyright statement within the code, or a requirement to redistribute the licensed software only under the same license (as in a <a href="/wiki/Copyleft" title="Copyleft">copyleft</a> license). One popular set of <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source software</a> licenses are those approved by the Open Source Initiative (OSI) based on their <a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Source Definition">Open Source Definition</a> (OSD).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Applications">Applications</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Applications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png/220px-121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png/330px-121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png/440px-121212_2_OpenSwissKnife.png 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="1646" /></a><figcaption>Open-source model application domains</figcaption></figure>
<p>Social and political views have been affected by the growth of the concept of open source. Advocates in one field often support the expansion of open source in other fields. But <a href="/wiki/Eric_Raymond" class="mw-redirect" title="Eric Raymond">Eric Raymond</a> and other founders of the <a href="/wiki/Open-source_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source movement">open-source movement</a> have sometimes publicly argued against speculation about applications outside software, saying that strong arguments for software openness should not be weakened by overreaching into areas where the story may be less compelling. The broader impact of the open-source movement, and the extent of its role in the development of new information sharing procedures, remain to be seen.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Open-source_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source movement">open-source movement</a> has inspired increased <a href="/wiki/Transparency_(humanities)" class="mw-redirect" title="Transparency (humanities)">transparency</a> and liberty in <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> research, for example <a href="/wiki/CAMBIA" class="mw-redirect" title="CAMBIA">CAMBIA</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Even the research methodologies themselves can benefit from the application of open-source principles.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It has also given rise to the rapidly-expanding <a href="/wiki/Open-source_hardware" title="Open-source hardware">open-source hardware</a> movement.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Computer_software">Computer software</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Computer software"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">Free and open-source software</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/GitHub" title="GitHub">GitHub</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Blender_3.3.0_screenshot.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Blender_3.3.0_screenshot.png/250px-Blender_3.3.0_screenshot.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Blender_3.3.0_screenshot.png/330px-Blender_3.3.0_screenshot.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Blender_3.3.0_screenshot.png/500px-Blender_3.3.0_screenshot.png 2x" data-file-width="1565" data-file-height="900" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Blender_(software)" title="Blender (software)">Blender</a>, an open-source 3D graphics editor</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">Open-source software</a> is software which source code is published and made available to the public, enabling anyone to copy, modify and redistribute the source code without paying royalties or fees.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/LibreOffice" title="LibreOffice">LibreOffice</a> and the <a href="/wiki/GIMP" title="GIMP">GNU Image Manipulation Program</a> are examples of open source software. As they do with proprietary software, users must accept the terms of a license when they use open source software—but the legal terms of open source licenses differ dramatically from those of proprietary licenses.
</p><p>Open-source code can evolve through community cooperation. These communities are composed of individual programmers as well as large companies. Some of the individual programmers who start an open-source project may end up establishing companies offering products or services incorporating open-source programs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Examples of open-source software products are:<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> (that much of world's server parks are running)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MediaWiki" title="MediaWiki">MediaWiki</a> (that Wikipedia is based upon)</li>
<li>Many more:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_free_and_open-source_software_packages" title="List of free and open-source software packages">List of free and open-source software packages</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_formerly_proprietary_software" title="List of formerly proprietary software">List of formerly proprietary software</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Google_Summer_of_Code" title="Google Summer of Code">Google Summer of Code</a>, often abbreviated to GSoC, is an international annual program in which Google awards stipends to contributors who successfully complete a free and open-source software coding project during the summer.  GSoC is a large scale project with 202 participating organizations in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  There are similar smaller scale projects such as the Talawa Project<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> run by the <a href="/wiki/Palisadoes_Foundation" title="Palisadoes Foundation">Palisadoes Foundation</a> (a non profit based in California, originally to  promote the use of information technology in Jamaica, but now also supporting underprivileged communities in the US)<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Electronics">Electronics</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Electronics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Open-source-hardware-logo.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Open-source-hardware-logo.svg/250px-Open-source-hardware-logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="125" height="131" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="538" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Hardware" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Source Hardware">Open Source Hardware</a> logo</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Open-source_hardware" title="Open-source hardware">Open-source hardware</a> is hardware which initial specification, usually in a software format, is published and made available to the public, enabling anyone to copy, modify and redistribute the hardware and source code without paying royalties or fees. Open-source hardware evolves through community cooperation. These communities are composed of individual hardware/software developers, hobbyists, as well as very large companies. Examples of open-source hardware initiatives are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Openmoko" title="Openmoko">Openmoko</a>: a family of open-source mobile phones, including the hardware specification and the <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenRISC" title="OpenRISC">OpenRISC</a>: an open-source microprocessor family, with architecture specification licensed under <a href="/wiki/GNU_GPL" class="mw-redirect" title="GNU GPL">GNU GPL</a> and implementation under <a href="/wiki/LGPL" class="mw-redirect" title="LGPL">LGPL</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>'s <a href="/wiki/OpenSPARC" title="OpenSPARC">OpenSPARC</a> T1 Multicore processor. Sun has released it under GPL.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arduino" title="Arduino">Arduino</a>, a microcontroller platform for hobbyists, artists and designers.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Simputer" title="Simputer">Simputer</a>, an open hardware <a href="/wiki/Handheld_computer" class="mw-redirect" title="Handheld computer">handheld computer</a>, designed in India for use in environments where computing devices such as personal computers are deemed inappropriate.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LEON" title="LEON">LEON</a>: A family of open-source microprocessors distributed in a library with peripheral <a href="/wiki/IP_core" class="mw-redirect" title="IP core">IP cores</a>, open <a href="/wiki/SPARC" title="SPARC">SPARC</a> V8 specification, implementation available under <a href="/wiki/GNU_GPL" class="mw-redirect" title="GNU GPL">GNU GPL</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tinkerforge" title="Tinkerforge">Tinkerforge</a>: A system of open-source stackable microcontroller building blocks. Allows control of motors and read out sensors with the programming languages C, C++, C#, Object Pascal, Java, PHP, Python and Ruby over a USB or Wifi connection on Windows, Linux and Mac OS X. All of the hardware is licensed under <a href="/wiki/CERN_Open_Hardware_License" class="mw-redirect" title="CERN Open Hardware License">CERN OHL</a> (CERN Open Hardware License).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Compute_Project" title="Open Compute Project">Open Compute Project</a>: designs for computer data center including power supply, Intel motherboard, AMD motherboard, chassis, racks, battery cabinet, and aspects of electrical and mechanical design.<sup id="cite_ref-OpenComputeProj_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OpenComputeProj-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Food_and_beverages">Food and beverages</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Food and beverages"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Voresol_label_medium.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Voresol_label_medium.png/125px-Voresol_label_medium.png" decoding="async" width="125" height="149" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Voresol_label_medium.png/188px-Voresol_label_medium.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Voresol_label_medium.png/250px-Voresol_label_medium.png 2x" data-file-width="470" data-file-height="559" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Vores_%C3%98l" class="mw-redirect" title="Vores Øl">Vores Øl – An Open Source Beer</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_and_Dakota_Meyer_sharing_a_beer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2731" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dakota_Meyer" title="Dakota Meyer">Dakota Meyer</a> drinking <a href="/wiki/White_House_Honey_Ale" title="White House Honey Ale">White House Honey Ale</a> in 2011. The recipe is available for free.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Some publishers of <a href="/wiki/Open-access" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-access">open-access</a> journals have argued that <a href="/wiki/Open_data" title="Open data">data</a> from <a href="/wiki/Food_science" title="Food science">food science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gastronomy" title="Gastronomy">gastronomy</a> studies should be freely available to aid <a href="/wiki/Reproducibility" title="Reproducibility">reproducibility</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A number of people have published creative commons licensed recipe books.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_cola" title="Open-source cola">Open-source colas</a> – cola soft drinks, similar to <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>, whose recipe is open source and developed by volunteers. The taste is said to be comparable to that of the standard beverages. Most corporations producing beverages keep their formulas secret and unknown to the general public.<sup id="cite_ref-octavio1_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-octavio1-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Free_Beer" title="Free Beer">Free Beer</a> (originally <i>Vores Øl</i>) – is an open-source beer created by students at the <a href="/wiki/IT_University_of_Copenhagen" title="IT University of Copenhagen">IT-University</a> in Copenhagen together with <a href="/wiki/Superflex" title="Superflex">Superflex</a>, an artist collective, to illustrate how open-source concepts might be applied outside the digital world.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Digital_content">Digital content</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Digital content"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:OK_LOGO_COLOUR_RGB.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/OK_LOGO_COLOUR_RGB.svg/125px-OK_LOGO_COLOUR_RGB.svg.png" decoding="async" width="125" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/OK_LOGO_COLOUR_RGB.svg/188px-OK_LOGO_COLOUR_RGB.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/OK_LOGO_COLOUR_RGB.svg/250px-OK_LOGO_COLOUR_RGB.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="873" data-file-height="1027" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Open_Knowledge_Foundation" title="Open Knowledge Foundation">Open Knowledge Foundation</a> logo</figcaption></figure>
<ul><li>Open-content projects organized by the Wikimedia Foundation – Sites such as Wikipedia and Wiktionary have embraced the open-content <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a> content licenses. These licenses were designed to adhere to principles similar to various open-source software development licenses. Many of these licenses ensure that content remains free for re-use, that source documents are made readily available to interested parties, and that changes to content are accepted easily back into the system. Important sites embracing open-source-like ideals are <a href="/wiki/Project_Gutenberg" title="Project Gutenberg">Project Gutenberg</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">Wikisource</a>, both of which post many books on which the copyright has expired and are thus in the <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a>, ensuring that anyone has free, unlimited access to that content.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_ICEcat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Open ICEcat (page does not exist)">Open ICEcat</a> is an open catalog for the IT, CE and Lighting sectors with product data-sheets based on <a href="/wiki/Open_Content_License" title="Open Content License">Open Content License</a> agreement. The digital content are distributed in XML and URL formats.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SketchUp" title="SketchUp">SketchUp</a>'s <a href="/wiki/3D_Warehouse" class="mw-redirect" title="3D Warehouse">3D Warehouse</a> is an open-source design community centered around the use of proprietary software that's distributed free of charge.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Waterloo_Stratford_Campus" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Waterloo Stratford Campus">University of Waterloo Stratford Campus</a> invites students every year to use its three-storey Christie <a href="/wiki/MicroTiles" title="MicroTiles">MicroTiles</a> wall as a digital canvas for their creative work.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Medicine">Medicine</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Medicine"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Pharmaceuticals – There have been several proposals for open-source pharmaceutical development,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which led to the establishment of the Tropical Disease Initiative<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the Open Source Drug Discovery for Malaria Consortium.<sup id="cite_ref-OpenWetWare_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OpenWetWare-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Genomics – The term "open-source genomics" refers to the combination of rapid release of sequence data (especially raw reads) and crowdsourced analyses from bioinformaticians around the world that characterized the analysis of the <a href="/wiki/2011_E._coli_O104:H4_outbreak" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 E. coli O104:H4 outbreak">2011 E. coli O104:H4 outbreak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenEMR" title="OpenEMR">OpenEMR</a> – OpenEMR is an ONC-ATB Ambulatory EHR 2011-2012 certified electronic health records and medical practice management application. It features fully integrated electronic health, records, practice management, scheduling, electronic billing, and is the base for many EHR programs.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Science_and_engineering">Science and engineering</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Science and engineering"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg/250px-Open_Access_logo_PLoS_white.svg.png" decoding="async" width="125" height="195" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="1000" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Open_access" title="Open access">Open access</a> logo</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Open_research" title="Open research">Open research</a></div>
<ul><li>Research – The <a href="/wiki/Science_Commons" title="Science Commons">Science Commons</a> was created as an alternative to the expensive legal costs of sharing and reusing scientific works in journals etc.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Research – <a href="/wiki/The_Open_Solar_Outdoors_Test_Field" title="The Open Solar Outdoors Test Field">The Open Solar Outdoors Test Field</a> (OSOTF)<sup id="cite_ref-osotf_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osotf-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is a grid-connected <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> test system, which continuously monitors the output of a number of photovoltaic modules and correlates their performance to a long list of highly accurate meteorological readings. The OSOTF is organized under open-source principles – All data and analysis is to be made freely available to the entire photovoltaic community and the general public.<sup id="cite_ref-osotf_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osotf-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Engineering – <a href="/wiki/Hyperloop" title="Hyperloop">Hyperloop</a>, a form of high-speed transport proposed by entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>, which he describes as "an elevated, reduced-pressure tube that contains pressurized capsules driven within the tube by a number of linear electric motors".<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Construction – <a href="/wiki/WikiHouse" title="WikiHouse">WikiHouse</a> is an open-source project for designing and building houses.<sup id="cite_ref-LaBarre_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaBarre-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kingsley_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kingsley-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Energy research – The <a href="/wiki/Open_Energy_Modelling_Initiative" title="Open Energy Modelling Initiative">Open Energy Modelling Initiative</a> promotes open-source models and open data in energy research and policy advice.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Robotics">Robotics</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Robotics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Open-source_robotics" title="Open-source robotics">Open-source robotics</a></div>
<p>An open-source robot is a <a href="/wiki/Robot" title="Robot">robot</a> whose blueprints, schematics, or source code are released under an open-source model.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Other">Other</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Other"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg/125px-VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg" decoding="async" width="125" height="115" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg/188px-VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg/250px-VIA_OpenBook_1_M.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="590" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/VIA_OpenBook" title="VIA OpenBook">VIA OpenBook</a> is an open-source hardware laptop reference design.</figcaption></figure>
<ul><li>Open-source principles can be applied to technical areas such as digital communication protocols and data storage formats.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-design_movement" title="Open-design movement">Open-design</a> – which involves applying open-source methodologies to the design of artifacts and systems in the physical world. It is very nascent but has huge potential.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_appropriate_technology" title="Open-source appropriate technology">Open-source appropriate technology</a> (OSAT) refers to technologies that are designed in the same fashion as <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">free and open-source software</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-buitenhuis_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buitenhuis-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These technologies must be "<a href="/wiki/Appropriate_technology" title="Appropriate technology">appropriate technology</a>" (AT) – meaning technology that is designed with special consideration to the environmental, ethical, cultural, social, political, and economic aspects of the community it is intended for. An example of this application is the use of open-source 3D printers like the <a href="/wiki/RepRap" title="RepRap">RepRap</a> to manufacture appropriate technology.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_learning&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Open-source learning (page does not exist)">Teaching</a> – which involves applying the concepts of open source to instruction using a shared web space as a platform to improve upon learning, organizational, and management challenges. An example of an Open-source courseware is the Java Education &amp; Development Initiative (JEDI).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other examples include <a href="/wiki/Khan_Academy" title="Khan Academy">Khan Academy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wikiversity" title="Wikiversity">wikiversity</a>. At the university level, the use of <a href="/wiki/Open-source_appropriate_technology" title="Open-source appropriate technology">open-source-appropriate technology</a> classroom projects has been shown to be successful in forging the connection between science/engineering and social benefit:<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This approach has the potential to use university students' access to resources and testing equipment in furthering the development of <a href="/wiki/Appropriate_technology" title="Appropriate technology">appropriate technology</a>. Similarly OSAT has been used as a tool for improving <a href="/wiki/Service_learning" class="mw-redirect" title="Service learning">service learning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>There are few examples of business information (methodologies, advice, guidance, practices) using the open-source model, although this is another case where the potential is enormous. <a href="/wiki/ITIL" title="ITIL">ITIL</a> is close to open source. It uses the <a href="/wiki/The_Cathedral_and_the_Bazaar" title="The Cathedral and the Bazaar">Cathedral model</a> (no mechanism exists for user contribution) and the content must be bought for a fee that is small by business consulting standards (hundreds of British pounds). Various checklists are published by government, banks or accounting firms.</li>
<li>An open-source group emerged in 2012 that is attempting to design a firearm that may be downloaded from the internet and "printed" on a <a href="/wiki/3D_printing" title="3D printing">3D Printer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-f20120823_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f20120823-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Calling itself <a href="/wiki/Defense_Distributed" title="Defense Distributed">Defense Distributed</a>, the group wants to facilitate "a working plastic gun that could be downloaded and reproduced by anybody with a 3D printer".<sup id="cite_ref-pcm20120824_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcm20120824-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Agrecol, a German NGO has developed an open-source licence for seeds operating with <a href="/wiki/Copyleft" title="Copyleft">copyleft</a> and created OpenSourceSeeds as a respective service provider. Breeders that apply the license to their new invented material prevent it from the threat of privatisation and help to establish a commons-based breeding sector as an alternative to the commercial sector.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Ecology" title="Open Source Ecology">Open Source Ecology</a>, farm equipment and global village construction kit.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="&quot;Open&quot;_versus_&quot;free&quot;_versus_&quot;free_and_open&quot;"><span id=".22Open.22_versus_.22free.22_versus_.22free_and_open.22"></span>"Open" versus "free" versus "free and open"</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: &quot;Open&quot; versus &quot;free&quot; versus &quot;free and open&quot;"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">Free and open-source software</a> (FOSS) or <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software#Overview" title="Free and open-source software">free/libre and open-source software</a> (FLOSS) is openly shared source code that is licensed without any restrictions on usage, modification, or distribution.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Confusion persists about this definition because the "free", also known as "libre", refers to the freedom of the product, not the price, expense, cost, or charge. For example, "being free to speak" is not the same as "free beer".<sup id="cite_ref-rmsdissent_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rmsdissent-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Conversely, Richard Stallman argues the "obvious meaning" of term "open source" is that the source code is public/accessible for inspection, without necessarily any other rights granted, although the proponents of the term say the conditions in the <a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Source Definition">Open Source Definition</a> must be fulfilled.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>"Free and open" should not be confused with public ownership (<a href="/wiki/State_ownership" title="State ownership">state ownership</a>), deprivatization (<a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalization</a>), anti-privatization (<a href="/wiki/Anti-corporate_activism" title="Anti-corporate activism">anti-corporate activism</a>), or <a href="/wiki/Transparency_(behavior)" title="Transparency (behavior)">transparent behavior</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/GNU" title="GNU">GNU</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/GNU_Manifesto" title="GNU Manifesto">GNU Manifesto</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Stallman" title="Richard Stallman">Richard Stallman</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gratis_versus_libre" title="Gratis versus libre">Gratis versus libre</a> (no cost vs no restriction)</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Software">Software</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Software"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">Open-source software</a></div>
<p>Generally, open source refers to a computer program in which the <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a> is available to the general public for use for any (including commercial) purpose, or modification from its original design. Open-source code is meant to be a collaborative effort, where programmers improve upon the source code and share the changes within the community. Code is released under the terms of a <a href="/wiki/Software_license" title="Software license">software license</a>. Depending on the license terms, others may then download, modify, and publish their version (fork) back to the community.
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_free_and_open-source_software_packages" title="List of free and open-source software packages">List of free and open-source software packages</a></li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_license" title="Open-source license">Open-source license</a>, a copyright license that makes the source code available with a product
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Open_Source_Definition" title="The Open Source Definition">The Open Source Definition</a></i>, as used by the <a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Initiative" title="Open Source Initiative">Open Source Initiative</a> for open source software</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_model" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source model">Open-source model</a>, a decentralized software development model that encourages open collaboration</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">Open-source software</a>, software which permits the use and modification of its source code</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/History_of_free_and_open-source_software" title="History of free and open-source software">History of free and open-source software</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_software_advocacy" title="Open-source software advocacy">Open-source software advocacy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_software_development" title="Open-source software development">Open-source software development</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source-software_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source-software movement">Open-source-software movement</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_video_game" title="Open-source video game">Open-source video games</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_open-source_video_games" title="List of open-source video games">List of open-source video games</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Business_models_for_open-source_software" title="Business models for open-source software">Business models for open-source software</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_open-source_and_closed-source_software" title="Comparison of open-source and closed-source software">Comparison of open-source and closed-source software</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Diversity_in_open-source_software" title="Diversity in open-source software">Diversity in open-source software</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MapGuide_Open_Source" title="MapGuide Open Source">MapGuide Open Source</a>, a web-based <a href="/wiki/Cartography" title="Cartography">map-making</a> platform to develop and deploy web mapping applications and geospatial web services (not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/OpenStreetMap" title="OpenStreetMap">OpenStreetMap</a> (OSM), a <a href="/wiki/Virtual_community" title="Virtual community">collaborative project</a> to create a <a href="/wiki/Free_content" title="Free content">free</a> editable map of the world).</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Hardware">Hardware</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hardware"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/RISC-V" title="RISC-V">RISC-V</a></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Agriculture,_economy,_manufacturing_and_production"><span id="Agriculture.2C_economy.2C_manufacturing_and_production"></span>Agriculture, economy, manufacturing and production</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Agriculture, economy, manufacturing and production"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_appropriate_technology" title="Open-source appropriate technology">Open-source appropriate technology</a> (OSAT), is designed for environmental, ethical, cultural, social, political, economic, and community aspects</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-design_movement" title="Open-design movement">Open-design movement</a>, development of physical products, machines and systems via publicly shared design information, including <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">free and open-source software</a> and <a href="/wiki/Open-source_hardware" title="Open-source hardware">open-source hardware</a>, among many others:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Open_Architecture_Network" title="Open Architecture Network">Open Architecture Network</a>, improving global living conditions through innovative <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_design" title="Sustainable design">sustainable design</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenCores" title="OpenCores">OpenCores</a>, a community developing <a href="/wiki/Digital_data" title="Digital data">digital</a> electronic <a href="/wiki/Open-source_hardware" title="Open-source hardware">open-source hardware</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Design_Alliance" title="Open Design Alliance">Open Design Alliance</a>, develops <a href="/wiki/Teigha" class="mw-redirect" title="Teigha">Teigha</a>, a software development platform to create engineering applications including <a href="/wiki/Computer-aided_design" title="Computer-aided design">CAD</a> software</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Hardware_and_Design_Alliance" title="Open Hardware and Design Alliance">Open Hardware and Design Alliance</a> (OHANDA), sharing open hardware and designs via free online services</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Ecology" title="Open Source Ecology">Open Source Ecology</a> (OSE), a network of farmers, engineers, architects and supporters striving to manufacture the <a href="/wiki/Global_Village_Construction_Set" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Village Construction Set">Global Village Construction Set</a> (GVCS)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenStructures" title="OpenStructures">OpenStructures</a> (OSP), a <a href="/wiki/Modular_design" title="Modular design">modular construction</a> model where everyone designs on the basis of one shared geometrical OS grid</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_manufacturing" title="Open manufacturing">Open manufacturing</a> or "Open Production" or "Design Global, Manufacture Local", a new <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomic" class="mw-redirect" title="Socioeconomic">socioeconomic</a> production model to openly and collaboratively produce and distribute physical objects</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_architecture" title="Open-source architecture">Open-source architecture</a> (OSArc), emerging procedures in imagination and formation of virtual and real spaces within an inclusive universal infrastructure</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_cola" title="Open-source cola">Open-source cola</a>, cola soft drinks made to open-sourced recipes</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_hardware" title="Open-source hardware">Open-source hardware</a>, or open hardware, computer hardware, such as microprocessors, that is designed in the same fashion as open source software
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_open-source_hardware_projects" title="List of open-source hardware projects">List of open-source hardware projects</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_product_development" title="Open-source product development">Open-source product development</a> (OSPD), collaborative product and process openness of open-source hardware for any interested participants</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_robotics" title="Open-source robotics">Open-source robotics</a>, physical artifacts of the subject are offered by the open design movement</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Seed_Initiative" title="Open Source Seed Initiative">Open Source Seed Initiative</a>, open source varieties of crop seeds, as an alternative to patent-protected seeds sold by large agriculture companies.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Science_and_medicine">Science and medicine</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Science and medicine"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Open_science" title="Open science">Open science</a>, the movement to make scientific research, data and dissemination accessible to all levels of an inquiring society, amateur or professional
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Open_science_data" class="mw-redirect" title="Open science data">Open science data</a>, a type of <a href="/wiki/Open_data" title="Open data">open data</a> focused on publishing observations and results of scientific activities available for anyone to analyze and reuse</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Science_Framework" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Science Framework">Open Science Framework</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Open_Science" title="Center for Open Science">Center for Open Science</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Lab_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Open Source Lab (disambiguation)">Open Source Lab (disambiguation)</a>, several laboratories</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-Source_Lab_(book)" title="Open-Source Lab (book)"><i>Open-Source Lab</i> (book)</a>, a 2014 book by Joshua M. Pearce</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-notebook_science" title="Open-notebook science">Open-notebook science</a>, the practice of making the entire primary record of a <a href="/wiki/Research_project" class="mw-redirect" title="Research project">research project</a> publicly available online as it is recorded</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Physics" title="Open Source Physics">Open Source Physics</a> (OSP), a <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Davidson_College" title="Davidson College">Davidson College</a> project to spread the use of open source code libraries that take care of much of the heavy lifting for physics</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Geospatial_Foundation" title="Open Source Geospatial Foundation">Open Source Geospatial Foundation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NASA_Open_Source_Agreement" title="NASA Open Source Agreement">NASA Open Source Agreement</a> (NOSA), an <a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Initiative" title="Open Source Initiative">OSI</a>-approved <a href="/wiki/Software_license" title="Software license">software license</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_open-source_software_for_mathematics" title="List of open-source software for mathematics">List of open-source software for mathematics</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_open-source_bioinformatics_software" title="List of open-source bioinformatics software">List of open-source bioinformatics software</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_open-source_health_software" title="List of open-source health software">List of open-source health software</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_open-source_health_hardware" class="mw-redirect" title="List of open-source health hardware">List of open-source health hardware</a></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Media">Media</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Media"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_film" title="Open-source film">Open-source film</a>, open source movies
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_open-source_films" title="List of open-source films">List of open-source films</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Cinema" title="Open Source Cinema">Open Source Cinema</a>, a collaborative website to produce a documentary film</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_journalism" title="Open-source journalism">Open-source journalism</a>, commonly describes a spectrum on online publications, forms of innovative publishing of <a href="/wiki/Online_journalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Online journalism">online journalism</a>, and content voting, rather than the sourcing of news stories by "professional" journalists
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open-source_investigation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Open-source investigation (page does not exist)">Open-source investigation</a></li></ul>
<dl><dd><i>See also: <a href="/wiki/Crowdsourcing" title="Crowdsourcing">Crowdsourcing</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Crowdsourced_journalism&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Crowdsourced journalism (page does not exist)">crowdsourced journalism</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Crowdsourced_investigation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Crowdsourced investigation (page does not exist)">crowdsourced investigation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Truther_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Truther (disambiguation)">trutherism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Historical_revisionism" title="Historical revisionism">historical revisionism</a> considered "fringe" by corporate media.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open-source_record_label" title="Open-source record label">Open-source record label</a>, open source music</li>
<li>"Open Source", a 1960s rock song performed by <a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Mushrooms" title="The Magic Mushrooms">The Magic Mushrooms</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_(radio_show)" title="Open Source (radio show)"><i>Open Source</i> (radio show)</a>, a radio show using open content information gathering methods hosted by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Lydon" title="Christopher Lydon">Christopher Lydon</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_textbook" title="Open textbook">Open textbook</a>, an open copyright licensed textbook made freely available online for students, teachers, and the public</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Library_(computing)#CAD_library" title="Library (computing)">CAD libraries</a> - such as <a href="/wiki/SketchUp" title="SketchUp">SketchUp</a> <a href="/wiki/SketchUp#3D_Warehouse" title="SketchUp">3D Warehouse</a> and <a href="/wiki/GrabCAD" title="GrabCAD">GrabCAD</a></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Organizations">Organizations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_source&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Organizations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Initiative" title="Open Source Initiative">Open Source Initiative</a> (OSI), an organization dedicated to promote open source</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Software_Institute" title="Open Source Software Institute">Open Source Software Institute</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Open_Source_Software" title="Journal of Open Source Software">Journal of Open Source Software</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Day" title="Open Source Day">Open Source Day</a>, the dated varies from year to year for an international conference for fans of open solutions from <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Developers%27_Conference" title="Open Source Developers&#39; Conference">Open Source Developers' Conference</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Development_Labs" title="Open Source Development Labs">Open Source Development Labs</a> (OSDL), a non-profit corporation that provides space for open-source project</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Drug_Discovery" title="Open Source Drug Discovery">Open Source Drug Discovery</a>, a collaborative drug discovery platform for <a href="/wiki/Neglected_tropical_diseases" title="Neglected tropical diseases">neglected tropical diseases</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Geeknet#SourceForge_and_OSDN" title="Geeknet">Open Source Technology Group</a> (OSTG), news, forums, and other <a href="/wiki/SourceForge" title="SourceForge">SourceForge</a> resources for IT</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_source_in_Kosovo" title="Open source in Kosovo">Open source in Kosovo</a></li>
